From what is observed from the accuracy, the Confusion Matrices and the F1 Scores, the
predictions need to be improved, to be considered a useful tool. Before improving a model, one
of the algorithms is chosen as the prediction model moving forward.
Between the two models, NB Classifier and RF Classifier with balanced data, the RF Classifier
reaches higher F1 scores for all classes except Class 2. Furthermore, the RF Classifier reaches
the high F1 Score for Class 5, after over-sampling the data, hence it is able to still find patterns
within this Class, which the NB Classifier is not. For these reasons, the RF Classifier is preferred
over the NB Classifier. Moreover, because the balanced data is better at predicting patterns
within the smaller classes in stead of being dominated by the larger classes, the over-sampled
model is preferred.
Having established which algorithm to use and with what data, some of the classes are merged.
This could potentially improve the performance of the algorithm, if it is done in a way, that
make sense in the real world. Then the model would possibly detect stronger patterns for each
class. Before the new model can be made, some phases of the CRISP-DM are revisited. These
phases are Business understanding, Data preparation and Modeling, which are conducted in the
following.
Revisited Business Understanding
It would be interesting to investigate, how the classifications change and whether the accuracy
improves by merging some of the classes. Real world observations are used as foundation for
arguing why the classes are merged the chosen way. The first is taken from the information
gathered from the interviewees for the qualitative analysis. Multiple of the interviewees work
within organizations that allow 1-2 days WFH each week (see Table 5 in Section 5.1). Therefore,
Page 100 of 238
==PAGE:110==
6
PROPOSED SOLUTION TOOL: A PREDICTIVE MODEL
Master Thesis
using a merge of Classes 1 and 2 makes sense based on what organizations are already doing.
Furthermore, a survey by Choudhury, Khanna, Makridis, and Schirmann (2022) from Harvard
University finds that three to four days WFH is the "sweet spot". Therefore, using a merge of
Classes 3 and 4 makes sense based on what is found in literature. Fionally, Classes 0 and 5 are
chosen to be kept separate, as they symbolize classes of respondents who prefer to either always
or never WFM, thus taking out the hybrid element. The new classes of WFH are: 0 days, 1-2
days, 3-4 days and 5 days, resulting in four classes in total.
Revisited Data Preparation
Before initiating the Modeling phase, the new classes are structured, extracting the optimal
features by using RFE, and finally over-sampling the data. The structuring of the new classes
has already been described, therefore the next step is feature selection.
Figure 19 visualizes the accuracy and number of features describing the target variable. It is
similar to Figure 18, except the accuracy is much higher this time (NB. this is before over-
sampling). This higher accuracy is accredited to the lower amount of classes compared to the
earlier models. After four features, the accuracy seems to find a stable accuracy until using eight
features where it increases again. To keep the model simple, and to avoid over-fitting by included
too many features, four features are used when modeling.
Figure 19: Number of respondents in each class
The following four features will be used in the models.
• To what extent do you agree or disagree that the following factors benefit your current
working from home? [I like the atmosphere in my home better than at work]
• To what extent do you agree or disagree that the following factors hinder your current
working from home? [I do not get to see my colleges or other people as much as I
would have liked to]
Page 101 of 238
==PAGE:111==
6
PROPOSED SOLUTION TOOL: A PREDICTIVE MODEL
Master Thesis
• 21 to 30 years
• Doctorate degree
Finally, the smaller classes are over-sampled, so all classes contain the same amount of observa-
tions. The final number of observations in each class in the training set is 447.
Revisited Modeling
This section provides a short description of the parameters used in the RF Classifier model.
The hyper parameter tuning for RF Classifier chooses the exact same parameters as the previous
hyper parameter tuning for RF Classifier with all six classes. These are displayed in Table 20.

Revisited Evaluation
The accuracy for the RF Classifier with balanced data is 0.45. The accuracy has been improved
from 0.28 (with balanced data) and 0.43 (with imbalanced). To say an accuracy is good or bad in
machine learning is subject to the problem. The fact that one of the chosen features for the model
is ’doctorate degree’ can generate some questions. Does the fact that a person has a doctorate
degree or not really influences how many days per week this person prefers to WFH? From
Table 11, only 3.2% of respondents in the data has a doctorate degree, and if they all have said
they wish to WFH 5 days a week, the model will believe all doctorates have that preference. This
example is to emphasize that the selected features do not necessarily contain the information
that can distinguish the classes most effectively.
Table 21 shows the Confusion Matrix of the model and Table 22 shows the F1 Scores of the
model. From both tables it appears that the model is struggling to classify Class 0 correctly. The
majority of predictions made for Class 0 are classified as belonging to Class 1-2 and the F1
Score for Class 0 is only 0.12. The same applies for Classes 3-4 and 5, where the majority of the
predictions are classified as belonging to Class 1-2. However, there are more correctly classified
predictions for Classes 3-4 and 5 than for Class 0. Moreover, a large part of the observations
belonging to Class 5 are predicted to belong to Class 3-4, which is of course incorrect. Finally,
the model still predicts that most observations belong to Class 1-2, which makes sense, as this
class is much more popular than the rest.

To gain a full overview of the data, which the model is trained on, the respondents’ answers to
each feature are visualized in Figure 20, 21, 22 and 23. These plots visually indicate how much
the respondents’ answers differ between each Class, for the four selected features.
Figure 20: Feature: I like the atmosphere
better at home
Figure 21: Feature: I miss my colleges
when WFH
Figure 22: Feature: 21-30 years
Figure 23: Feature: Doctorate degree
From the two first figures, Figure 20 and 21, there is a clear relation between the answers and the
preferred number of days WFH. In Figure 20, the respondents should specify to which degree
they feel the atmosphere is better at home than at the office. Respondents who answered 5 to this
question (they like the atmosphere at home much better), are also the largest pool who wants to
WFH 5 days. As the answers for the question approach 1, the fewer days per week they prefer to
Page 103 of 238
==PAGE:113==
6
PROPOSED SOLUTION TOOL: A PREDICTIVE MODEL
Master Thesis
WFH. The same tendency is observed in Figure 21, just the other way around; respondents who
answered 5 to this question (they miss their colleges to a high degree when WFH), are also the
largest pool who wants to WFH 0 days. As the answers for the question approach 1, the more
days per week they prefer to WFH. Looking at the patters for these two features, it seems as
the model would be good at predicting Classes 0 and 5. Looking at the Classes next to them,
there is still a relatively large amount of people who answer the same, and when answering 4,
it is almost the same amount. Moreover, when the models are evaluated, the applied test set is
imbalanced, so even though the model’s ability to distinguish the classes has improved, the test
data still contains large classes for Class 1-2 and 3-4.
Figure 22 and 23 show the respondents’ answers across the classes for the binary features
21-30 years and Doctorate degree. These two features do not show as clear relation to the
preferred number of days WFH like the previous two features. It is important to notice for
these two features, that the blue respondents (who answered 0) in the figure, are both the red
respondents from the other classes (answered 1) and all the other age groups and educational
degrees. Therefore, only the respondents who have answered 1 are considered for both features.
The preferences among the days WFH for the age feature is still following the same distribution
that was seen in Figure 17: Class 1-2 are the most popular days to WFH, closely followed by
Class 0 an 3-4. For the last feature, Doctorate degree, the majority of respondents prefers to
WFH 0 days when having a doctorate degree, and only very few prefer the remaining classes.
In summary, the final model for the solution proposal is the RF Classifier, using over-sampled
data with the prediction classes: 0 days, 1-2 days, 3-4 days and 5 days. The final RF Classi-
fier achieved an accuracy of 0.45. The Confusion Matrix showed that the model classified no
predictions for Class 0 in Class 5 and vice versa, which means that the model is able to find
patterns that can distinguish these two extreme classes. However, overall the final model is still
struggling to correctly classify the observations, as only 45% were classified correctly.
Judging the model’s ability to function as a managerial tool for FTDMs based on the numeric
results, it is concluded that the model is not suitable due to the high degree of misclassifications.
For the model to provide the needed value for organizations, it should provide highly accurate
results, which would show a reliability to the leaders deciding an organization’s WFH policies.
Moreover, for the FTDM to use the results of the model, these need to accommodate the actual
preferences of the employees to some extend. Due to the low classification accuracy of the
model, the results of the model are not deemed satisfactory for practical use.
Although the ML model is deemed unsuitable for solving the identified challenge in practice on
the basis of the numerical results, there are other underlying aspects to the results of the model
that may influence its applicability as a solution tool for FTDMs. These aspects together with
the general methods and results of the model are discussed in the following section.
Page 104 of 238
==PAGE:114==
7
DISCUSSION
Master Thesis
7
Discussion
After qualitative analysis of the interview-data, choosing a challenge and proposing a solution in
the form of a predictive model, there are multiple factors to be discussed. This includes methods
and results from both the qualitative and quantitative parts of the study as well as the combination
of the two. This, together with a reflection of using mixed methods in an academic study, is
presented in the following.
7.1
Using mixed methods
During this project, the scope and focus changed multiple times. It was established from the
beginning that the study would be a mixed methods study, and what data would be used for the
quantitative part. For the story of the thesis to come together, the aim and focus of the quantitative
study was refined and altered throughout the time of the thesis. For both the qualitative and
quantitative methods, the other had be to taken into account in all scoping decisions to make sure
that the two analyses would fit together and create one cohesive report, solving the same problem.
This was quite challenging at times - especially because the secondary data for the quantitative
study was already conducted. This meant that there was a restriction to tailor the questions
for the survey to fit with the findings of our qualitative study, which in the end impacted the
applicability of the final machine learning model. The fact that the secondary data was given
meant that the target variable for the prediction model was determined before going into the
qualitative study. This affected the decision made in regards to the focus of qualitative study
throughout the thesis. Due to the comprehensiveness of the qualitative data, there were many
interesting directions to go with the analysis. Due to the solution tool already being established,
there were clear boundaries to the focus of the qualitative analysis, which was both beneficial
and restrictive, as it forced a certain perspective onto the analysis but also gave a clear direction,
which simplified the analytic process.
Throughout the thesis work, the importance of including a human aspect in the interpretation of
quantitative results became clear. The chosen ML model could to some extend predict the target
variable, but it was with human eyes that it was possible to evaluate whether the predictions
could actually obtain value in the real world. With the ML model, the aim was to predict personal
preferences of people based on their replies to survey questions. Taking a problem, which is
about personal preferences of humans, boiling it down to numbers and trying to solve it with
quantitative methods will always be difficult and will create questions about whether the model
adequately represents the people on whom it is based. The details of the human behavior are
lost and the solutions that are given, need thorough interpretation by the right set of eyes before
being validated.
Page 105 of 238
==PAGE:115==
7
DISCUSSION
Master Thesis
There are concrete methodological aspects for the qualitative and quantitative methods separately
that need to be discussed in order to determine the validity of this study, which is done in the
next sections.
7.2
Qualitative findings and methods
Data collection
For this project, qualitative methods were used for primary data-gathering and subsequent
data-analysis. The aim of the study was to investigate how first-time daily managers (FTDM)
experience the task of managing a hybrid team - an area that has not before been studied in detail.
To investigate this area, it was required to understand the managers’ situations and feelings
towards hybrid work and gain in-depth insights into the challenges they meet due to working
within a HWM. To gain these insights and achieve detailed data for the analysis, an exploratory
approach was taken, and for this, the qualitative methods were viewed as most appropriate.
For data-collection, semi-structured interviews were conducted. Unstructured interviews were
viewed as too open, as some relevant topics to ask about were already known from literature and
the scope of the project. Structured interviews were not viewed as a relevant method for data-
collection, as the close-ended questions of this method would arguably not allow for exploration
of relevant topics that may appear during the interviews.
For the primary data-collection, the authors’ networks were to find relevant participants. The
interviewees joined the study on a voluntary basis. Therefore, the interviewees may have been
managers with some extend of confidence in their role and maybe also managers who did not
see the biggest issues of managing hybrid teams. If this is the case, it may have influenced the
degree of challenges reported by the interviewees. Throughout the interviews, insights were
gained into the topic and problems within, which may have resulted in us leading the interviews
more in a certain direction as the interviews progressed. This also means that the interviewees
were not asked the same follow-up questions. This lies within what can be expected from
the semi-structured interview format, but will have had an influence on the outcomes of the
interviews as the topics discussed within each were varying to some extend.
In the end, data was gathered from seven managers and one of each of their employees (except
for Int 7 -no employees were available). The interviews with employees were conducted to verify
the statements of the managers. The initial idea had also been to include the statements from the
employees at times, where they elaborated on relevant aspects for the analysis, but due to time
constraints, this was not done. It may also have mixed up the findings and made the analysis less
focused - after all the aim was to study the challenges experienced by the managers.
Throughout the interviews, it was at times difficult to get something out of the interviewees, when
asking directly about the challenges they felt in their role as managers due to the HWM. The
Page 106 of 238
==PAGE:116==
7
DISCUSSION
Master Thesis
reluctance to open up may be due to some degree of professional pride, where they interviewees
(consciously or unconsciously) feel uncomfortable to open up about their own shortcomings.
Because of this, a lot of the interview-data became about other things than what was challenging
for the managers. Therefore, it was an essential part of the following analysis to be aware of
the underlying interpretations of the statements which nevertheless were able to shed light on
challenging aspects for the interviewed managers. More experience in conducting interviews
may have given us a better interview technique and could possibly have resulted in a higher
quality of data-gathering.
All interviews were conducted in Danish to make it easier for the interviewees to speak freely
without having to translate their thoughts into English. This was believed to be the best approach
to get as unfiltered statements from the interviewed managers as possible. This meant that the
statements had to be translated before including them in the report. Because it is difficult to
translate spoken language into something that is exactly the same as in the native tongue, it may
have slightly altered the meaning of the statements compared to what was said. This however,
was assessed to not have an influence on the validity of the analysis or the comprehensiveness of
the conclusions and interpretations made from the interview-data.
The qualitative study was a cross-case study, where multiple cases were collected and com-
pared. When possible, the specific findings from the cases were taken from the particulars and
generalized into larger conclusions, spanning across cases. To have generalizability in data,
there must be a degree of similarity within data-providers (i.e. the interviewees). Moreover,
the number of interviewees must be large enough so that a certain data-saturation is achieved,
where patterns emerge from the information given by the interviewees. These aspects were
achieved to some degree in the study. The similarity between interviewees was assessed to be
high on relevant parameters, as these were set as selection criteria for the interviewees. The
data-saturation was also achieved but only to some degree. There were a large portion of the
identified challenges which were reported by a number of interviewees, which shows that these
were common challenges across multiple cases. Moreover, many of the aspects highlighted in
each interview, in relation to managing a hybrid team, were to a great extend similar. Therefore,
these aspects showed a satisfying degree of saturation. However, when diving into the analysis
and identifying the types of HWMs for the interviewees, it was found that only one interviewee
had a remote-first HWM. Because of this, the conclusions made in regards to how FTDMs
function within this type of work model are not as strong as the conclusions drawn for the
office-first HWM, where conclusions were based on data collected from four interviewees. The
number of interviewees having an office-occasional HWM was also on the smaller side, which
made it a bit difficult to observe clear patterns between these, thus making it difficult to draw
clear conclusions on the challenges specific to this type of HWM. To verify whether the patterns
found between the types of HWMs in the analysis, further studies need to be conducted with
Page 107 of 238
==PAGE:117==
7
DISCUSSION
Master Thesis
more informants working within each type of HWM.
Selecting challenges for further analysis
Due to the immense amount of collected data, there was not room in the analysis to go deep
into explanations and interpretations for all challenges and the interrelations with other chal-
lenges. This meant that some were chosen over others. Selecting challenges for further analysis
was based on different arguments. These include; excluding challenges only reported by one
interviewee, identifying key challenges based on the types of HWMs of the interviewees; using
the key challenges as focal point for analysis and then only diving into analysis related to key
challenges and challenges connected to them. These selection methods were used as they seemed
reasonable to keep us from compromising information relevant to address the research questions.
It is difficult to say whether there were better ways to select relevant challenges but of course
there is a possibility of this.
If other selection methods were used, it may have resulted in a different selection of challenges,
which may have given a different picture of the difference in challenges due to the type of HWM.
Findings from the analysis
The findings from the qualitative analysis showed a list of 29 challenges for FTDMs managing a
hybrid team, and tried to explain the occurrence of these by the type of HWM for the interviewed
managers. Compared to the challenges found in literature for managers in general working
within a HWM many of the same were found in this study. From Table 2 (table of advantages and
challenges of a HWM found in literature) some of the most common challenges found in litera-
ture are connected to knowledge sharing, trust in employees, technical facilities, social isolation
and everyday social interactions. In this study, knowledge sharing was mentioned as a challenge
due to the HWM by all interviewees. Although the remaining three challenges were reported by
some of the interviewees, they are far from the most common challenges among the interviewed
managers. It may therefore be argued that the challenges of the FTDM in a HWM differs from the
ones by managers in general working within a HWM. In the study, planning, work arrangements
and conducting hybrid meetings are more frequently mentioned as challenges than i.e. trust.
Planning is found to have increased in difficulty and the hybrid way of conducting meetings is
challenging for the FTDM. These challenges are connected to practical everyday tasks for the
FTDMs, which may be why they are reported by many in this study but have not been empha-
sized in studies investigating challenges for managers in general. This indicates that the results
from this thesis can contribute to increasing the understanding of the challenges specific to FT-
DMs and that some challenges are in fact specific to the responsibilities and novelty of this group.
In the analysis investigating whether the type of HWM could explain why some manages experi-
ence the challenges they do, the findings suggested that FTDMs working within an OF work
Page 108 of 238
==PAGE:118==
7
DISCUSSION
Master Thesis
model would experience more challenges than those working within an OO or a RF work model.
These FTDMs would especially be challenged by social challenges, trust and monitoring. They
would also have a more negative attitude towards working within a HWM than FTDM from the
other two types of HWMs. Other challenges would relate to the task of planning and establishing
rules, but these were also experienced by FTDMs from other types of HWMs. Additionally,
the findings suggested that FTDMs working within a RF HWM would experience very few
challenges. Related to these findings are a number of aspects that threaten the conclusions. First,
the number of interviewees for the three types of HWMs were four (OF), two (OO) and one
(RF). Due to there being evidently more interviewees for the OF HWM, it is much more likely
that there will be reported an overweight of challenges for this type. Thus the many challenges
may not be due to this group being more challenged but because of the larger sample size for
the study. Having only one interviewee for the RF HWM makes it difficult to say anything
about the tendencies of challenges for FTDMs within this type of HWM. This fact weakens
the conclusions made in regards to the FTDMs within a RF work model significantly. Second,
even though the results suggest a difference between how challenging the interviewees report
finding managing hybrid teams, it may not be determined by their type of HWM. The three
interviewees Int 1, Int 3 and Int 5, who all have an OF HWM, are found to dislike managing a
hybrid team, and find many challenges in doing so. These three interviewees also happen to be
females, whereas the rest, who have a predominantly positive attitude towards the HWM, are all
men. This explanation for the differing attitudes and experienced challenges is just as reasonable
as the explanation of the type of HWM. Therefore, it will take further research on the topic to
establish exactly what influences the challenges of FTDMs managing hybrid teams.
Bias
When it comes to the bias in the qualitative study, there is both some connected to the data
collection and the analysis. The bias associated with the interviews can come from both the
interviewees and the interviewers (us) (Saunders et al., 2007, p. 156). Interviewees may be
reluctant to share some types of information - for instance things regarding their own abilities as
managers, as mentioned in the discussion section about data collection. If the interviewees have
a feeling that they will be put in a bad light because of their responses to the interview questions,
it may cause them to hold back information. It was tried to prevent this by establishing from the
beginning of each interview that they would be anonymous in the report. This may have taken
some of the bias from the interviewees, but they may still not have wanted to lose face in front of
us during the interviews, which could have contributed to some degree of bias in their responses.
Interviewee bias can also be created due to the interview-process. Semi-structured interviews can
be an intrusive process, where participants are asked to be vulnerable about sensitive topics. In
our case, the vulnerability for the interviewees lies on opening up about the challenges of living
up to their relatively new role as managers, which can be quite sensitive for some. Therefore,
Page 109 of 238
==PAGE:119==
7
DISCUSSION
Master Thesis
even though the interviewees participated willingly, they may not be comfortable with the
unstructured exploration of certain themes, thus choosing not to reveal certain aspects of the
challenges they face as FTDMs in a HWM (Saunders et al., 2007, p. 326).
Interviews are subjective in nature, and the information will come from the thoughts and opin-
ions of the interviewee. However, there will be an element of interviewer bias in the comments,
tone or non-verbal behavior of the interviewer, which may create a bias in or alter the way
the interviewee responds to questions (Saunders et al., 2007, p. 326-327). For the data col-
lection in this thesis, the interviewees were sometimes reluctant to go much into the essence
of their challenges. This sometimes resulted in us asking questions in a more leading manner
than what is perceived as "correct" behavior when conducting interviews. This was viewed as
necessary, but may have skewed the interview-data slightly towards our own perceptions at times.
Bias connected to the qualitative analysis is mainly caused by personal bias of the person
analyzing the data. This is created by the researcher’s personal agenda affecting their ability to
present the data analysis in a trustworthy manner (Miles et al., 2020, p. 289). To try and decrease
personal bias, the authors have talked with each other about the different interpretations of the
data during the analysis, such that at least they were on the same page about the interpretations.
When identifying the challenges, it was done in collaboration between the two of us to draw out
as much meaning from the formulation of each challenge as possible.
7.3
Quantitative findings and methods
The size of the data
The impact of dataset size on classification performance is a well discussed topic. Several
research have proposed measurements that can identify the minimum number of necessary
samples to achieve the desired accuracy (Andonie, 2010; Shawe-Taylor, Anthony, & Biggs,
1993), but there are still no agreed definition of what constitutes a small dataset. It is known,
that the more data the models can train upon the better, as the data potentially contain more
generalized patterns. On the other hand, small dataset are said to contain less details, consistency
and struggles to generalize patterns in training data (Althnian et al., 2021). This might have
an influence on the final model, as the data that was used to train the model consisted of 1778
observations (over-sampled data). It would be incorrect to assume that this is the case, but it
would also be naive to ignore this knowledge, since the Class 0 from the original data consisted
of only 48 observations before random over-sampling.
Page 110 of 238
==PAGE:120==
7
DISCUSSION
Master Thesis
Machine learning methods
In the process of creating a predictive model that can explain the number of days an employee of
knowledge work prefers to WFH, multiple machine learning methods have been used. The ML
methods consists of the final ML algorithm, and the approaches of optimizing the model. In this
section, the following methods will be discussed: the Recursive Feature Elimination (RFE) and
Over-sampling.
Recursive Feature Elimination
Before selecting which features to include in the model using RFE, the optimal number of
features to include was investigated. This was also done with the RFE that investigates how the
number of features to include in a model influence the accuracy. This was visualized in Figure
19. The figure showed that the optimal number of features to include in the model was 19 as the
highest accuracy was achieved at this point. In spite of this, only four features were selected, as
the accuracy reached a stable state, until eighth features were included and then the accuracy
increased again. It can be argued, that by only including four features, the model does not reach
its full potential when an higher accuracy is reached with 19 features. Nonetheless, four features
were selected as including 15 features more, would most likely result in overfitting the model,
and the accuracy would only increase with approximate 0.01.
Over-sampling
It has been identified that the data was imbalanced, as the smallest class, Class 0, contained 46
observations and the largest class, Class 2, 375 observations. To avoid bias towards predicting
Class 2 in the model, it was necessary to balance the classes. To balance the classes, Over-
sampling was used. A drawback of this approach is when it is randomly copying the exact same
observation, the likelihood of over-fitting the model increases. In this way, the model might
construct rules based on the replicated observation that apparently are accurate, but actually just
one replicated example (Alberto et al., 2018, p. 85). This is important to have in mind, but it does
not change the fact that over-sampling was implemented to avoid the large bias towards Class 2.
The final results of the predictive model
There is no agreed numeric definition, or numeric threshold, that separates a good model from a
poor one, as it is subjective to the problem.
Overall, the model is struggling to classify the observations correctly, as only 43% are correctly
classified. Even though feature selection, hyper parameter tuning and over-sampling were imple-
mented, which contribute to improving a ML algorithm, the performance of the model increased
only a little. In the end of the analysis, it was concluded that the model was not suitable for FT-
Page 111 of 238
==PAGE:121==
7
DISCUSSION
Master Thesis
DMs to use as a decision tool, due to the high degree of misclassifications. This section seeks to
understand why the model fails to reach the desired outcome based on the findings in the analysis.
When the model classifies predictions incorrectly, it could be a matter of answers for the features
contradicting the preferred number of days WFH. It may be that an employee want to WFH five
days a week due to personal conveniences, but in reality the employee misses their colleagues
and does not like the atmosphere at home as much as in the office. This would then mean that
WFH five days a week is not optimal for the working conditions of the employee - although
it may be what they would choose if being asked. The fact that the ML model is not able to
predict with higher accuracy than 0.45 may therefore be a smaller issue for the applicability
of the model than anticipated. A person like the hypothetical employee would in the case of
the predictive model skew the predictions and decrease the accuracy of the model, since their
response falls way out of the patterns found by the model. However, this point is difficult to
prove and therefore difficult to take into account when evaluating the applicability of the ML
model as a solution tool for FTDMs.
Is the data suitable for a predictive model?
There is a saying: A machine learning model is only as good as the data it is fed. The data itself
has a high quality in terms of the structure of the variables, outliers, missing values, and the data
information. The references to this saying, is more about: Can this data be used to predict the
number of days, an employee of knowledge work should WFH? The data was not collected for
this specific purpose, and therefore this discussion is relevant in order to see if it is even possible
that such a prediction can be done successfully.
The four final features the RFE selected was: ’I like the atmosphere in my home better than
at work’, ’I do not get to see my colleges or other people as much as I would have liked to’,
’21 to 30 years’ and ’Doctorate degree’. From Figure 20 and 21, the atmosphere feature and
missing colleges showed a clear tendency of the target variable and respondents’ answers to
the features. If the respondents preferred working only a few days from home, they were more
likely to have answered that they miss their colleges when WFH and not liking the atmosphere
at home more than at the office. The same was true the other way around if the respondents
answered they prefer to work a lot from home. For the age group and doctorate features, the
relations were not as clear. If the age group and doctorate features are important features to
explain the target variable, the excluded features might either have similar patterns as the chosen
features, be contradicting the patterns that the model finds or contain less information that can
distinguish the classes. The survey data is based on people’s preferences, which is individual, so
even though two people have answered they wish to WFH the same number of days and have
Page 112 of 238
==PAGE:122==
7
DISCUSSION
Master Thesis
the same preferences of one aspect, they may not have the same preference of another aspect.
Therefore, the model then struggles to find a pattern, which is most likely the reason why the
models struggle to correctly classify the observations.
Due to the fact, that the data was not collected for the purpose it was used for, the variables
are not structured with the intention to predict the target variable. Moreover, some of the data
is build upon preferences, which also can increase the complexity of the problem, as trying to
predict something that is very individual can be challenging.
To investigate if machine learning can be used to predict the number of days an employee of
knowledge work prefers to WFH, either more variables are needed or a new survey should be
constructed, where the intention is to predict this. Additional variables could for example be
formulated as ’In percentage, how many of your tasks can be solved from home?’, or some
variables concerning the respondent’s personality traits. A research conducted by Gavoille and
Hazans (2022) identifies that there is a link between personality traits and willingness to WFH.
It would therefore be interesting to investigate how much it would improve the model to include
personality traits, that has showed a relation with the preferred working arrangement.
It is likely that not all organizations will be willing to implement the tool - even if a sufficient
accuracy was achieved. As mentioned in Section 6.1, there lies an assumption for the applicability
of the model. Because the model tries to give information that can help the manager structure
the work arrangements to fit with the preferences of employees, the organization must give
up their control of the number of days that employees are required to work from the office.
If organizations do this, they will consequently change their HWM and incorporate less strict
HWM into their organization. Thus, an office-first work model may very well be difficult to
sustain. It may be a lot to ask of organizations that they change their hybrid work structure,
which presents a limitation for the use of the model. In summary, the final model presented in
this thesis is at its currently state not suited to use as a management tool for structuring a hybrid
team’s work arrangements. Nonetheless, it would not be unrealistic to improve the model with a
larger amount of or more tailored data, turning it into a decision tool for managers to use for
structuring a hybrid team’s work arrangements. The implementation of the tool would require an
open mind toward changing their HWM from organizations with an office-first HWM, as the
tool in its current state is not applicable within such strict work models.
7.4
Mixed methods reflection
In light of the work done in this thesis, what does it take to mix methods and work in the inter-
section between hard and soft science? First of all, it takes trust in others’ academic/professional
abilities. Often, like in this thesis, people working on projects have different competencies,
and are therefore not able to validate each others’ work. This necessitates that people take
Page 113 of 238
==PAGE:123==
7
DISCUSSION
Master Thesis
responsibility for their part of the work and let go of the need to control what others are doing. It
requires that the team members are able to fill each other in on aspects that are important for
the overall understanding of the work, but leaves the details to the individual people working
on the different components of the project. It can take some time to build the necessary trust
between the team members and what we experienced in this thesis is that building the needed
trust requires both a common social understanding and a sense of security that the other person(s)
is capable of carrying their part of the weight. Due to the relatively short time horizon of the
thesis, it was necessary to build this trust early on. This was possible due to the intensity of
the work when being together daily for extended periods of time, but it was also thanks to the
common attitude towards the thesis process. We new that for the mixed methods to succeed,
including the amount of work that needed to be done, we had to be able to split up, which
required trusting the other person’s work.
Having different competencies and taking on the role of ’expert’ in different fields but at the
same time being able to ’speak the same language’, enabled us to support and compliment
each other in the aspects that overlapped without having to be deep involved the entirety of
the work within both methods. We found it to be essential when conducting mixed methods
work, that there is some degree of common understanding and at least an understanding of the
surface aspects of the method that the other person(s) is working on. Without this, it will be dif-
ficult to create a project which makes sense from both perspectives and is aiming at the same goal.
Conducting a mixed methods study takes time. It takes time and energy to frame the problem
in a way that makes sense from both perspectives and it takes work digging into two whole
methods instead of sticking with just one. The resulting work will be quite comprehensive and
take up a lot of space like seen in this project. Due to the time it takes to frame the project
and correctly conduct multiple methods, the level of detail within each method and the quality
of the findings may have been compromised slightly. Concluding on this, perhaps we have
wanted to say too much with this thesis. We have wanted to give the qualitative and quanti-
tative parts equal depth and weight in the project instead of choosing one as the leading and
including the other as supportive or additional for relevant aspects. Using one of the methods
as more primary focus might have given the project a bit more focus and allowed there to
be a deeper dive into the data from that method. Although it might have made sense to focus
more on one method, some degree of detail was necessary to display a correct use of the methods.
Page 114 of 238
==PAGE:124==
8
CONCLUSION
Master Thesis
8
Conclusion
This project is an exploratory cross case, mixed methods study investigating the management of
hybrid teams. The aim of the study is to (1) identify challenges that first-time daily managers
(FTDMs) experience when managing a hybrid team, (2) assess whether the type of HWM in
an organization can explain which challenges FTDMs experience and (3) investigate whether
machine learning (ML) can be used to create a solution tool for one of the identified challenges.
Through the duration of this project, qualitative methods were used to obtain primary data. The
primary data was collected from seven FTDMs — four with an office-first HWM, two with
an office-occasional HWM and one with a remote-first HWM. The data was coded, analyzed
and presented in accordance with qualitative methods. Furthermore, quantitative methods were
applied to secondary data from a survey developed by Kirchner et al. (2022) and conducted by
Epinion. Thus, both qualitative and quantitative methods have been applied in the formation of
the report to answer the research questions presented herein.
Initially, a literature review was conducted to establish a common understanding of the existing
knowledge related to the thesis problem. Diving into the literature, the first research question
was investigated:
What is currently known from literature about the challenges that managers in general face
when managing hybrid teams?
This literature review revealed a list of eight organizational challenges and five individual
challenges that are caused by having a HWM. These were selected from literature due to more
than one paper having found such challenges. The three most frequently mentioned organizational
challenges were: knowledge sharing, mistrust in employees and technical limitations, and the
three most frequently mentioned individual challenges were social isolation, lack of social
interaction and longer hours.
The literature did not specify the level of management that would experience each challenge or
which type of HWM was used for the studies. It did revealed that many FTDMs are not very well
equipped to carry out their responsibilities, due to lack of training and preparation for the role.
The effects of being new to management have not been investigated in a hybrid work setting
before. This revealed a gap in existing literature that opened up for an interesting perspective of
this exploratory study, which are address though the next research question:
Which challenges does a hybrid work model bring for first-time daily managers working within
knowledge-based organizations? And can the type of hybrid work model explain which
challenges first-time daily managers experience when managing a hybrid team?
The analysis resulted in 29 challenges for FTDMs in KBOs when managing hybrid teams.
These challenges were found from the overall codes relating to: Management Responsibilities,
Page 115 of 238
==PAGE:125==
8
CONCLUSION
Master Thesis
Meetings and Chats, Social Needs, Success of a HWM and Employee Demands. Four key chal-
lenges were found to be experienced by FTDMs from all three HWM types in the study. These
key challenges include: Customizing work arrangements for employees, Knowledge sharing is
challenged, Hybrid meetings and Reaching out virtually is less natural.
The analysis showed that many challenges are only experienced by the interviewees with an OF
work model, fewer but still a large portion are also experienced by the interviewees working
within an OO work model and that quite few are experienced by the interviewee working within
a RF work model. This suggests that it may be more challenging for a FTDM to work within
an OF work model than within both an OO and a RF work model. The analysis showed that
interviewees within an OF work model generally had a more negative attitude towards the
HWM due to the difficulties in knowledge sharing and virtual interactions, which they react
to in a way that excludes their employees when WFH. This may be due to FTDMs within an
OF work model not practicing telework themselves, they do not experience the benefits of a
HWM. For interviewees in OO and RF work models, the case is different - herein, managers
too reap the benefits of WFH. Interviewees from all types of HWMs view flexibility as one of
the greater benefits that a HWM gives their employees. On the downside, giving the employees
this flexibility, FTDMs have to customize the work arrangements for their employees which
increases the complexity of their role.
The analysis suggested that there is a connection between the challenges experienced by the
interviewees and the type of HWM they work within. This pattern may perhaps be generalized to
be true for FTDMs in general when managing hybrid teams, but to say this confidently, further
investigation with a larger sample size must be conducted.
The findings do not present unambiguously results to answer the research question of whether
the type of HWM can explain the challenges faced by FTDMs. The perspective used for the
analysis was to look at the types of HWM, but as it turns out, it may just as well be the gender
that decides the challenges experienced by an FTDM working within a HWM — or possibly
something entirely else. Therefore, to establish the origin of the challenges, further investigation
is required.
Which of the identified key challenges makes sense for knowledge-based organizations to solve?
And can this challenge be solved using a predictive model based on the data from Epinion?
The key challenge chosen to create a solution for is: Customizing work arrangements for
employees.
To translate the challenge regarding work arrangement into the quantitative data, the variable
"From now on, if your workplace allows it, how many days per week would you like to work
from home?" was selected as the target variable. The final model using the RF Classifier with
Page 116 of 238
==PAGE:126==
8
CONCLUSION
Master Thesis
over-sampling, achieved an accuracy of 0.45, which corresponds to 45% of the observations
being classified correctly.
The FTDM would need fact-based results to accommodate the preferences of the employees,
the team and the organization. Due to the low accuracy score of the final model, this does not
satisfyingly live up to the task of solving the chosen challenge. The low accuracy score will
create mistrust from upper-management regrading how much the work arrangement would
represent the actual preferences, deeming the model an undesirable solution tool.
The ML model may also be affected by whether the Epinion data is suited for predicting the pre-
ferred number of days WFH for employees. It is a complex task to predict personal preferences
based on the given data, as it does not take the human aspect behind the numbers into account.
Based on the numerical results of the final machine learning model, and evaluating how much
value the results potentially provides the FTDMs, the individual employees and the organization,
it is concluded that this predictive model is not a suitable tool for FTDMs to use when structuring
the work arrangement for a hybrid team.
Although the model is not suited as a solution tool for the chosen problem, the quantitative
results still show that the atmosphere at home and missing employees are the factors that have
the highest impact when determining how many days per week employees prefer to work from
home.
What key challenges do first-time daily managers in knowledge-based organizations
experience when managing a team within a hybrid work model? And can human resource
officers in knowledge-based organizations use a predictive model based on the data from
Epinion to prevent one of the identified key challenges?
In summary, the study finds four key challenges that FTDMs experience when managing a
hybrid team. These are: Customizing work arrangements for employees, Knowledge sharing is
challenged, Hybrid meetings and Reaching out virtually is less natural. The machine learning
model, based on the Epinion data, was found to be unable to solve the key challenge: Customizing
work arrangements for employees due to unsatisfactory accuracy of the predictions made by the
model.
Page 117 of 238
==PAGE:127==
9
IDEAS FOR FUTURE WORK
Master Thesis
9
Ideas for future work
In the following section, relevant aspects that would be relevant to investigate further or elements
that could improve the proposed solution are presented.
The qualitative analysis from Section 5 suggests that the type of HWM implemented in an orga-
nization might be able to explain the challenges of managing hybrid teams for FTDMs. Since
the interviewees having an office-occasional and remote-first HWM were under-represented
in the interview-data, a study with higher representation of these types should be conducted to
see if the findings align with what is suggested trough the qualitative analysis of this thesis. In
order to make the findings generalizeable, an analysis with more data should be conducted. The
data to analyze could both be qualitative or quantitative. Having a larger pool of respondents or
interviewees would provide a rich, contextualized understanding of whether or how the type of
HWM can explain the experience of managing hybrid teams as a FTDM.
Another aspect to consider, is collecting more quantitative data to feed the Machine Learning
model with. Without over-sampling, the model only included 1054 observations, which were
imbalanced towards working two days from home. The smallest class consisted of 46 obser-
vations without over-sampling, which is arguably not enough to make generalizations of this
class. Collecting more data could potentially improve the performance of the models, or at least
indicate if the data in general is suitable to predict the preferred number of days WFH from the
data.
Another perspective in terms of improving the performance of the ML models, could be collect-
ing new quantitative data. This should be collected based on trying to solve this specific challenge
FTDMs are experiencing: Using ML to structure a hybrid team’s work arrangement in a knowl-
edge based organization. This would require an extensive qualitative study that specifically asks
the respondents questions that are aiming more towards predicting the target variable. The results
from the qualitative study would be used as a foundation to developed survey questions that are
suitable for predicting the target variable. Finally, the survey sample should be conducted so it
represents the Danish work force in knowledge work.

APPENDIX: QUALITATIVE METHOD
Master Thesis
A
Appendix: Qualitative method
A.1
Message on LinkedIn for interviewee acquirement
Er du daglig leder og har erfaringer med at lede hybride teams? Så vil vi gerne interviewe dig og
en af dine medarbejdere!
COVID-19 har sat sine spor på mange arbejdspladser, hvor hybridarbejde er blevet en del af
hverdagen. Mange studier undersøger hvordan ansatte bedst muligt arbejder hybridt, men der er
brug for fokus på, de udfordringer lederne står overfor.
Vi, Astrid og Emma, vil i vores kandidat speciale på Danmarks Tekniske Universitet (DTU)
undersøge hvordan organisationer kan hjælpe deres daglige ledere til at lede hybride teams. Det
gør vi igennem dataanalyse af både kvantitativt og kvalitativt data.
Vores vejleder er Christine Ipsen, der forsker i ledelse og organisering af hybrid-arbejde.
Vi søger daglige ledere samt en af deres medarbejdere til at hjælpe os med at besvare spørgsmål
vedrørende deres oplevelse af at lede og indgå i hybride teams.
Interviewet vil bestå af spørgsmål som I vil få tilsendt inden interviewet, og vil tage omkring en
½ time. Det kan både være online eller på din arbejdsplads, hvad der passer dig/jer bedst.
Kontakt os enten her på linked-in, eller skriv på mail:
s174324@student.dtu.dk
s171013@student.dtu.dk
/Astrid Helene Erecius og Emma Jespersen
#masterthesis #hybridwork #hybridarbejde #hybridmanagement #telework #distancemanage-
ment #firstlinemanagers #ledelse #DTU

==PAGE:134==
A
APPENDIX: QUALITATIVE METHOD
Master Thesis
A.2
Interview guide, version 1
Introduktion
• Hvad er dit navn?
• Hvad er din stilling?
• Hvor mange medarbejdere har du under dig?
• Hvor længe har du været leder, og hvor længe af den tid har du været leder for et hybrid
team?
• Kan du prøve at forklare kort hvordan en normal arbejdsdag ser ud?
• Synes du, at den ledelse, du yder for dem som arbejder hjemme, er den samme som for
dem, som arbejder på kontoret?
Det hybride arbejde
• Hvordan er jeres opsætning/rammer af hybridarbejde?
• Er der dig, der beslutter i hvilket omfang dine medarbejdere arbejder hjemmefra eller er
det en beslutning, der er taget fra toppen?
• Hvornår arbejder man hjemme? Er det opgaven eller stedet, der kommer først?
• Kan du beskrive din rolle/ansvar som leder i dit team?
• Hvordan sørger du for at medarbejderne er koordinerede?
• Hvad er rammerne for kommunikationen i dit team?
• Hvordan opbygger du tillid mellem dig og dine medarbejdere?
• Hvordan vil du karakterisere den type af hybridarbejde som det team du leder arbejder
under? (evt. Introducer de forskellige typer)
Oplevelsen af hybridarbejde
• Hvad ser du som værende den/de største udfordring(er) ved at lede hybridarbejde?
• Føler du at der er ting du kan gøre for at komme dette til livs?
• Føler du at din organisation prøver at komme disse til livs?
• Hvad ser du som værende den/de største fordel(e) ved at lede hybridarbejde?
Page 125 of 238
==PAGE:135==
A
APPENDIX: QUALITATIVE METHOD
Master Thesis
• Føler du at det primært er en fordel eller udfordrende at lede et hybrid team?
• Hvordan har din egen trivsel været i forbindelse med ledelse af hybride teams?
• Er dette anderledes end da du ledte teams under fysisk tilstedeværelse?
Værdier og ledelsesstil
• Hvilke værdier har du som leder og synes du at disse afspejles i dit team?
• Har disse værdier ændret sig da du gik fra on site til hybrid ledelse?
• Hvordan vil du beskrive din ledelsesstil?
• Har denne ændret sig da du gik til at lede hybridt?
Arbejdsopgaver
• Inden for et framework som definerer en leders opgaver ud fra planlægning, kontrol,
ledelse og organisering, hvor meget tid bruger du så på hver især relativt til hinanden? Vil
du illustrere dette?
• Hvordan prøver du at motivere dine medarbejdere?
• Har du indført ledelsesværktøjer for at gøre det nemmere for dig selv at lede hybride
teams – dette kan være til at måle performance, planlægning af hybridt arbejde, se hvornår
medarbejdere møder ind, etc.

Det hybride arbejde
• Hvordan er jeres opsætning/rammer af hybridarbejde?
• Er der dig, der beslutter i hvilket omfang dine medarbejdere arbejder hjemmefra eller er
det en beslutning, der er taget fra toppen?
• Hvornår arbejder man hjemme? Er det opgaven eller stedet, der kommer først?
• Hvordan sørger du for at medarbejderne er koordinerede?
• Hvad er rammerne for kommunikationen i dit team?
• Hvordan opbygger du tillid mellem dig og dine medarbejdere?
• Hvordan giver du dine medarbejdere feedback på deres arbejde?
• Taler du eksplicit med dine medarbejdere om hvordan det går med at arbejde hjemmefra?
Oplevelsen af hybridarbejde
• Hvad ser du som værende den/de største udfordring(er) ved at lede hybridarbejde?
• Hvad ser du som værende den/de største fordel(e) ved at lede hybridarbejde?
• Føler du at det primært er en fordel eller udfordrende at lede et hybrid team?
Værdier og ledelsesstil
• Hvilke værdier har du som leder og synes du at disse afspejles i dit team?
• Hvad ligger du vægt på ved den måde du leder på?
• Hvordan vil du beskrive din ledelsesstil?
• Hvordan prøver du at motivere dine medarbejdere?
• Inden for et framework som definerer en leders opgaver ud fra planlægning, kontrol,
ledelse og organisering, hvor meget tid bruger du så på hver især relativt til hinanden? Vil
du illustrere dette?
• Til sidst vil vi være lidt frække og spørge om du måske har en kollega med samme
baggrund som dig selv, som du kunne henvise os til?

A.11
Validation table
Objectivity/Confirmability
Methods and procedures are described in detail
!
It is possible to follow how data was collected, processed, displayed
!
Conclusions are explicitly linked with displayed data
!
Method is recorded clearly enough to be replicated buy others
!
Awareness of biases and how these may have come into play
!
Rival conclusions have been considered
!
Data is retained and able to analyze by others
!
Reliability/Dependability/Auditability
Research questions are clear and research design is consistent with them
!
Researcher’s role has been described
!
Findings show meaningful parallelism across data sources
!
Basic paradigms and analytic constructs are clearly specified
!
Data was collected across a full range of appropriate respondents etc.
!
Intercoder agreement checks have been made with adequate results
-
Data quality checks have been made
!
Observers’ accounts converge when expected to
!
Forms of peer review are in place
!
Internal validity/Credibility/Authenticity
Descriptions are content-rich, meaningful and "thick"
!
The report makes sense and seems convincing or plausible
!
Triangulation among methods and data sources
-
Presented data is linked to prior or emerging theory
!
Findings are clear, coherent and systematically related
!
Confirmation procedures for conclusions are described
(!)
Any areas of uncertainty have been identified
(!)
Negative evidence was sought
!
Rival explanations have been actively considered
!
Conclusions were considered to be accurate by the original participants
N/A
External validity/Transferability/Fittingness
The characteristics of sample persons are described to permit comparison
!
Specifies limits to sample selection and examines ability to generalize
!
Sample is theoretically diverse enough to encourage broader applicability
!
Findings include adequately "thick" descriptions to assess transferability
!
Readers report that the findings are consistent with their own experiences
!
Concluded outcomes are applicable in comparable settings
(!)

sige, hvis jeg skal være meget ærlig, altså der hvor jeg nogen gange kan sidde og
overveje, det er om det de løser derhjemme, måske kunne være løst på 7 timer i
stedet for 8 timer. For jeg har jo ikke nogen jordisk chance for at vurdere hvor meget
kaffe, vasketøj, gå med hunden, snak med konen, der går i den i løbet af en dag.
Det ved jeg jo ikke. ” 00.13.01
Knowledge
sharing work
best on-site
“jeg synes også den uformelle sparring og vidensdeling kollegaerne imellem fungerer
bedst fysisk. Så jeg tror at jeg synes niveauet 1-2 dage om ugen er maks” 00.03.55
Does not think
that managing
from home works
“nej jeg er jo ikke ret meget leder for dem når de arbejder hjemmefra. Mange af dem,
ser jeg der om morgen ni til halv ti og så hører jeg ikke mere fra dem“00.04.31
The HWM is
more of an offer
for the employees.

WFH gives
happier
employees

works well
for employees

østen. I forventning om at det virkelig betyder noget at have været tæt på folk og

D
Appendix: Interview transcriptions (managers)
Before every interview, the following disclaimer was read aloud:
Dette interview foregår i forbindelse med vores, Astrid og Emma, kandidat speciale i efteråret
2022. Projektet handler om ledelse af hybridarbejde med fokus på at finde områder med ud-
fordringer og kortlægge hvor virksomheder kan give deres dagligere ledere nogle værktøjer
til at forbedre deres ledelsesopgave. Vi laver disse interviews for at få et indblik i hvordan
dagligere ledere håndterer ledelsesopgaven under hybridarbejde og hvordan det modtages af
Page 153 of 238
==PAGE:163==
D
APPENDIX: INTERVIEW TRANSCRIPTIONS (MANAGERS)
Master Thesis
deres medarbejdere.
Dit navn vil ikke fremgå i rapporten, men dine udtalelser fra interviewet kan blive inkluderet
som citater med mindre fortrolige elementer fremgår. Det håber vi at du er ok med.
Er det okay at vi optager interviewet?
Det er Emma der primært vil stå for at stille spørgsmål, og Astrid tager notater imens.
The transcriptions are a mix between notes taken during the meetings and quotes derived from
the recordings. The notes are marked with a hyphen and quotes are in italics so the reader is able
to tell the difference between the two. Questions by the authors are marked in bold.
D.1
Transcription for interview with Int 1
Hvad er din stilling?
- Hun har været faglig leder i 1.5 år - ikke haft medarbejder under sig – men er lige blevet
offiecielt leder med personale under sig i september (så ca. 1,5 måned inden interviewet).
- hun har QA inden for innovation men også ACM life cycle management – innovation er
man tilknyttet projekt – life cycle management er mere operational og arbejder sammen med
produktionen i malaysia, Kina, USA og Mexico – dagligt samarbejde, ift ændrnig af produkter
(materiale, design osv).
- Har kun været leder for hybrid team. De har to roller: 1. Kigger alt dokumnetation igennem fra
et kvalitetsperspektiv (QA: auality assurance), 2. risk management rolle, fungerer produktet så
det er sikkert for bruger.
- Organisationen er en matrix org, hvor de har forskellige funktioner, men der er meget projekt-
baseret, så de bliver delt ud på forskellige projekter fra Int 1s team.
- Det betyder også at man sidder meget alene med opgaven, når man er ude på et projekt.
“det er faktisk meget projektbaseret, så man sidder meget alene med opgaven, så det er vigtigt at
vi har de her møder (teams møder) hvor man sådan lige “hov hvad sker der omkring med de
andre”.” 00.07.47
“de referer til mig, men man kan sige at meget af deres daglige sparring er også med deres
projektleder” 00.08.11

Hvor mange medarbejdere har du under dig?
- 5 under sig, og de bliver 4 til første december. 4/5 er ingeniører,
Hvor længe har du været leder, og hvor længe af den tid har du været leder for et hybrid
team?
- Delvist, vi kom stille og roligt tilbage efter corona – hun har ikke prøvet “normal ledelse” før.
Kan du prøve at forklare kort hvordan en normal arbejdsdag ser ud?
Synes du, at den ledelse, du yder for dem som arbejder hjemme, er den samme som for
dem, som arbejder på kontoret?
- De kører 1-1 én gang om ugen, face-to-face ca. En halv time
“vi kører 1:1 en gang om ugen, og det ser vi helst bliver på stedet, når vi tager de her 1:1 for det
fungerer bedst at holde 1:1 face-to-face. Det er ca en halv time pr medarbejder" 00:05:09
- Det fungerer bedst face-to-face: pga af kropssprog, kan bedre mærke personen – kan have svært
ved at tolke hvad der bliver sagt igennem kroppen.
- Hendes fornemmeste opgave er at medarb. Trives så hun vil gerne kunne mærke hvordan de har
det.
- Teams møder hvor de kører rundt om bordet, er der nogle highlights, udfordringer - kører en
gang om ugen.
Er hun ordstyrer?
- Ja hun har lavet struktur fra hendes side – men det er et frit forum –> hun starter med sig selv,
og hun har disse highlights - “jeg har oplevet det s” –> matrix organisation så det kører mest
projekt orienteret
- så hendes medarbejdere kan sidde med mange forskellige medarbejdere i organisationen.
“vi kører teams møder, hvor vi kører rundt om bordet, hvor vi kigger på sådan hvad er det vi
laver, highlights, udfordringer eller nogle ting vi skal håndtere. Og så skal vi finde ud af – er det
sådan noget meget opgavespecifikt eller er vi ovre i sådan et procesniveau. Det er typisk en gang
om ugen vi kører dem” 00:06:27
Til ugentlige teams møder: “det er mig der har struktureret dem, der er lagt en struktur fra min
side af. Det er der brug for. Men der er meget sådan frit forum” 00.07.02
Til ugentlige teams møder: “Det kan godt være at jeg kan finde på at sige sådan: “nu starter
mødet, nu gør vi det her, jeg kan starte med mig selv“ det er altid en god ice-breaker – for

Det hybride arbejde
Hvordan er jeres opsætning/rammer af hybridarbejde?
Er der dig, der beslutter i hvilket omfang dine medarbejdere arbejder hjemmefra eller er
det en beslutning, der er taget fra toppen?
Hvornår arbejder man hjemme? Er det opgaven eller stedet, der kommer først?
“vi foretrækker man er her ude fire gange om ugen og så er der den fleksibilitet at man kan
arbejde hjemme en dag“ 00.09.30
man kan selv vælge hvilken dag. “men det skal helst ikke ligge fast” 00.09.42
“jeg tror især det er for at imødekomme det behov der er opstået under corona at man kan lige
tage 1,5 time af is in kalender og blokere (...) den fleksibilitet som man fik sig under corona
og ligesom bibeholde den fleksibilitet.” 00.09.48 “så det er for at imødekomme medarbejderne”
00.10.10
“vi har en regel at når man er hjemme, så skal man helst have kamera på, men det er optional.
Det gør også, fordi der er meget med kropssproget i den måde man kommunikerer på, at jeg kan
bedre mærke og føle, hvordan mine medarbejder har det, når der er på kontoret lige overfor mig.
Hvis der er kamera på så er det nogenlunde det samme, men hvis der ikke er kamera på, så kan
jeg have lidt svært ved at tolke det der bliver sagt” 00:05:28
“jeg har brug for at vide også hvordan den pågældende medarbejder har det” 00:06:00
“jeg tænker at min fornemmeste opgave er at mine medarbejdere trives. Selvfølgelig at de kan
lave deres opgaver, men også lige så meget at de trives. Så det er vigtit for mig ligesom at kunne
-mærke dem” 00:06:05
- Der er en dag om ugen man godt må arbejde hjemmefra – man vælger selv hvilken dag, de ser
at man arbejder her 4 dage om ugen
- Den fleksibilitet under corona, vil man gerne bibeholde, for at imødekomme medarbejdere og
ikke nødvendigvis organisationen.
- Ømt punkt: der er ingen der bryder sig om at blive mikromannagemt
– det er ledelse under ansvar, forventer der bliver leveret gode opgaver - når det er sagt skal der
stadig være en følning af hvad der sker når der arbejdes hjemmefra

Master Thesis
– der er behov for 2 min nogle gange som er nemmest når man er samlet samme sted.
“der er ingen der bryder sig om at blive micromanaged, forstået på den måde at der er ingen der
bryder sig om at ens leder ved præcis hvilke opgaver man sidder med på den pågældende dag –
det er altså ledelse under ansvar - forstået på den måde, at jeg forventer at du leverer det du
leverer. Hvordan og hvor meget tid du bruger på det er fuldstændig underordnet. Det vigtigste er
at du leverer de opgaver.“ 00.10.36
“Når det så er sagt er det også nødvendigt at have en føling af hvad det er der sker, og det er
bare rigtig svært, når man er hjemme. Og det gælder også lige så meget, når jeg er hjemme. Så
har jeg sådan lidt svært ved ok, hvordan er vi og hvad rør på sig? Fordi der er også nogle gange
behov for, at man bare kan gå ind og sige, “hey har du lige 2 minutter? Jeg vil gerne snakke med
dig”, og det er nemmere, når man er på stedet. Så jeg vil ikke sige det er en udfordring, men det
er bare noget nemmere, når man er samlet et sted.” 00.11.00
“det er også meget forskelligt hvilken medarbejder jeg har med at gøre. Nogle er jeg lidt trykkere
ved at ved sådan ok, hvis de har brug for en dag hjemme, “ok gør det, du behøver ikke fortælle
mig det”, og så har jeg andre hvor jeg er mere sådan “jeg har brug for at du fortæller mig, når
du er hjemme”. Og det har med at gøre, at nogle er bare mere selvstændige end andre. Så det er
også hvor selvstændig den medarbejder er” 00.11.40
“har jeg en bedre relation til den medarbejder, har jeg en bedre føling af hvad medarbejderen
laver, hvor faglig stærk medarbejderen er, jo mere vil jeg sige, “jo så gør du det” (altså arbejder
hjemme)“ 00.12.23
- Det er meget forskelligt ift medarejder – nogle er hun mere tryg ved at arbejde hjemmefra,
andre har hun brig for at de fortæller hende hvornår de arbejder hjemme
– hvor selvstændige medarbejderen er og hvordan personen tidligere har leveret. Har hun en
bedre relation til medarbejderen, hvor selvstændige de er så er hun mere tryg ved at lade dem
arbejde hjemmefra
- Ambu har sagt de må arbejde på denne måde med 4-1. Når det så er sagt, så har de nogen som
arbejder hjemme to dage om ugen.
“det er mere det der med at vi giver fleksibiliteten, men vi har en forventning om at man er her.
De fleste dage. ” 00.13.14

“det bliver fremlagt som at nu har jeg brug for at sætte mig derhjemme og arbejde sådan helt

“Man skal ikke negligere, at hvis du ikke kan få det til at fungere personligt, mistrives du, og så
kan du heller ikke fungere på arbejdet. Så det er også noget med motivation og det tilhørsforhold

- Hvorfor vil de arbejde hjemmefra: Mest det personlige behov, hun har en opfattelse af at det
ikke altid er fordi de vil være fokuseret men ofte er personlige gøremål.
Hvordan sørger du for at medarbejderne er koordinerede?
- Nej – det styrer de helt selv. De har næsten alle sammen været her under hybride forhold, så de
beslutter selv hvornår arbejde hjemmefra – hvis de selv er arrangør af et møde, så er der større
sandsynlighed for at det lykkes hvis de er til stede.
- Hvis det er et diskussion eller lyttemøde kan det godt gøres hjemme.
- Om koordinering (om Int 1 har sat et system eller procedurer op for hvordan det skal foregå):
“det styrer folk helt selv. Også fordi de har mere eller mindre alle sammen været her under
corona tiden eller har prøvet noget lignende et andet sted, så de ved hvad der skal til” 00.14.59
“de mærker selv efter og beslutter hvornår de har lyst til at være her selv og hvornår de kan tage
den hjemmefra. Og grunden til at jeg siger det er, at de ved godt at hvis de selv er arrangør af et
møde, og hvis det er et arbejdsmøde, så er der nok en større sandsynlighed for at det lykkes, hvis
de er til stede. Det er svært at styre et møde hjemmefra” 00.15.18
“hvis det er sådan et diskussionsmøde, eller sådan et møde, hvor man kun lytter, så kan det være
i orden (at være hjemme)” 00.15.36
Hvad er rammerne for kommunikationen i dit team? Er der forskel på hvordan i kan tale
om?
- Hun har bedt om at gøre det tydeligt i sin kalender hvor man er – eksternt for afdelingen at
kunne følge med i om man er tilstede eller hjemme – helst ugen inden men det er ikke “ulovligt”.
- Man behøver ikke at fortælle at man er hjemmefra, men man skal sætte det ind i kalenderen.
- Men også internt i gruppen – hvis alle i ens arbejdsopgave er hjemme, er der så behov for at
være til stede.

Hvis en er hjemmefra som har relevante inputs, føles det så naturligt for hende at spørge

- Ja, det vil hun sige, hun tilgår dem mere hvis der er kamera på: nemmere sige “hvad siger du?”

Hvordan opbygger du tillid mellem dig og dine medarbejdere?
- Følger meget op på dem for at skabe tillid – nu har hun et team der performer godt.

Hvordan giver du dine medarbejdere feedback på deres arbejde?
Taler du eksplicit med dine medarbejdere om hvordan det går med at arbejde hjemmefra?

ikke gå godt?“ (...) det ville aldrig være set som noget positivt” 00.36.22

Har du oplevet at de er ineffektive? “ja” 00.37.34
- det har ikke hjulpet at tage snakken med vedkomne
“vi har en der er sygemeldt. Og jeg vil gerne sige at jeg tror at det med at arbejde hjemmefra
har gjort det endnu sværere for hende at komme tilbage. Fordi det er nemmest for hende. Vi
tog en snak omkring, hvad skal der til for at du kommer herind? Hvordan kan vi få dig mere
herud? Og hun kunne ikke overskue hvad der skulle til for at komme herud. Så spørger jeg,
hvad er det der gør det? Så siger hun at det er det der med at skulle ud hjemmefra, det med at
gøre sig klar og indstille sig på at hun skal herud sådan rent praktisk, og der er så meget med
det at skulle møde folk. Det synes hun var virkelig hårdt. Så det bryder hun sig ikke om.” 00.37.46
“det kan være farligt at sende folk for meget hjem. Man falder ind i en eller andet trygheds sådan
boble derhjemme, som man har svært ved at kommelidt ud af. ” 00.38.52

herhjemme“ 00.39.21
Oplevelsen af hybridarbejde
Hvad ser du som værende den/de største udfordring(er) ved at lede hybridarbejde? - Hvis
hun spørger om det er ok at arbejde hjemme - så føler hun at medarbejderen bliver lidt skeptisk.
- Hun vil tage en snak om det hvis un føler de er ineffektive eller falder lidt i baggrunden af
arbejdet.
- Hvordan har det været efter snakken: det har ikke rigtig hjulpet, har en sygemeldt medarbejder,
hun føler det at arbejde hjemmefra har gjort det endnu svære at komme herud, hun kunne ikke
overskue at komme herud, da det at gøre sig klar og indstille sig på at skulle herud rent praktisk
og at møde sine medarbejdere.
- Hvis hun havde været sygemeldt hvis hun har været herude fuldtid føler Int 1 at det har ikke
styrket hende i at hun fik lov til at arbejder mere og mere hjemmefra.
- Når man kom tilbage fra COVID, så skulle man lære at være på igen og social. –> kan det have

Hvad ser du som værende den/de største fordel(e) ved at lede hybridarbejde?

Værdier og ledelsesstil Hvilke værdier har du som leder og synes du at disse afspejles i dit
team?
- Der er en forventning om at hun bakker dem fuldt op når noget går galt og kan hjælpe dem,
støttende leder og opbakkende.
- Hun har en forventing om når de kommer til dem, så skal der handles på problemet.
- Hun sætter pris på: gennemsigtighed (er der noget der ikke fungere, så bliver det addresseret),
tillid (de opgaver der bliver lavet, lever op til det der forventes af dem), faglighed (man er faglig
stærk).
Tager du dage hjemmefra selv?
- Det er pisse hårdt at arbejde hjemmefra, for der er en forventning fra medarbejdere at hun er
der.
Hun føler det er sværre at tage fat i hende når hun arbejder hjemme
“jeg har en forestilling om at der er en forventning fra mine medarbejdere om at jeg er her“
00.34.30
Handler det om at hun er en ny leder?
- Handler mere om at være synlig – man er mere usynlig når man er hjemme.
“jeg tror som leder er man nødt til at være synlig” 00.35.16
- EDP – kompetence udvikling, hvordan kommunikerer jeg bedre som leder osv.
- Samtaler man tager for at se hvordan medarbejder kan styrkes både fagligt og personlige –
konverterer sin 1-1, da de skal have gjort sig nogle tanker om fremtid personligt og fagligt.
- Så 1-1 er mere det daglige - så følger de op ugentligt på det der bliver sagt i 1-1.
- Int 1 skal undersøge hvorfor er det medarbejeder ikke trives og hvordan kan hun ændre det.
- Hun mangler lidt at lave en struktur mellem de to forskellige møder, hvordan de adskilles og
sættes op.
- Int 1 vil være mere på hvis det er in person ift. Mødet eller relationen.
“hvis vi tager det virtuelt, igen, så har jeg en forventning om at så er der kamera på, og så vil jeg
også mere overlade det til den pågældende medarbejder. Så vil jeg sige “ok, hvis du gerne vil
have at vi gør det her virtuelt, så føler jeg også at du har et ansvar i at få det her til at fungere”.
På den måde ville jeg nok være lidt mere på når det er in person“ 00.32.05
“der er en forventning om at når du er på en arbejdsplads, at så giver ud dig også tid til at tale
med andre om hvordan det går” 00.40.07
Hvordan vil du beskrive din ledelsesstil? “jeg tror at der er en forventning om at jeg bakker
dem fuldt på når der er behov for det, og at de er trygge ved at gå til mig, hvis det går galt“

Hvilken type leder:
- Dem opbakkende leder, hands on: hun har sagt jeg har tillid til i laver jeres opgaver, og behøver

projektledere. Så jeg snakker med dem om hvordan går det på projektet, uden at sige hvordan
går det med Anna i projektet, og hvordan går det med projektet, for så kommer de selv med
bekymringer eller med ting der ikke fungerer eller ting der virkelig fungerer. (. . .) så der er fint,
hvordan vi ser det internt, men jeg har brug for sådan at have en føling på hvordan bliver det set
udefra. Det ved mine medarbejdere i øvrigt ikke“ 00.44.01

ledelse og nu også meget nedad.

vi laver den antagelse at hjemmearbejdet ikke påvirker arbejdet, så vil fordelingen være uændret.

- Dem der er mere hjemme, fylder meget herude - så der er en god balance.

deadlines (et par dage)

Oplevelsen af hybridarbejde
Hvad ser du som værende den/de største udfordring(er) ved at lede hybridarbejde?
- Det er svært at lave tommelfingerregler som gælder for alle, da det er meget forskelligt hvad
der fungerer for folk. Man kan ikke rigtig lære alle over en kam.
- Derfor er flekstiden hos os god. Det fungerer rigtig, rigtig godt.
- Jeg tror ikke man skal underkende værdien af at kunne hente sine børn og så arbejde en time
ekstra om aftenen. Det giver bare nogle fede friheder.
- Under corona var det forfærdeligt at være hjemme hele tiden
- Jeg tror ikke hybridarbejde kun er nemt, men jeg har bare kun mærket de positive ting, der er
forbundet med det.
- Det her med tab af kontrol og folk der ikke leverer har jeg ikke oplevet. De ting der opstår må
man tage hånd om og tage en samtale om.
- Der er en konsekvens af at alting skal ind i en kalender og man kan ikke lige tage to min til at
sige noget, så mange møder er også bare for at tage et par små ting, så to min ting bliver til en
halv time.
- Nogle gange skal noget langt ud i fremtiden for at kunne tale om nogle små ting. Mødekulturen
er gået amok
- 8-17 arbejdstid smuldrer lidt når man er derhjemme, også hvis folk tager noget tid i løbet af
dagen på andet, så der sker noget med at man ikke har fri på samme måde
“jeg føler bare, og det kan godt være at det bare er en følelse, men det føles som om at det er
sværere at tune sig til et andet menneske, når du sidder over for dem. Så spørgsmålene bliver
nok stillet på en anden måde, men jeg prøver at være på meget menneske som overhovedet muligt
- også over teams, så man ikke bliver for finans-robot agtig, men det er svært for mig at vurdere
om det opleves anderledes.” 00.28.35
“det er meget svært at lave sådan nogle tommelfingerregler, som er bedst for alle. Og det bliver
du jo nødt til på et eller andet niveau, for det er jo en arbejdsplads, folk skal også møde ind, men
det er meget personligt hvad man egentlig har det bedst med, så det er rigtig svært at skære den
bare sådan *krwittt*, nu er det bare på den her måde for alle.” 00.29.30
“altså coronatiden, hvor man var hjemme fuld tid, det var frygteligt, men det her fungerer faktisk
rigtig, rigtig godt. Og jeg tror ikke man skal underkende værdien af at kunne hente sin datter fra
skole og tage til spejder med sin søn eller sådan et eller andet og så arbejde en time om aftenen”
